# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox DOM Event Dispatch Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a DOM event (e.g., click) is dispatched through the Firefox event system in mozilla/gecko-dev. Find C++ source files implementing: the event creation, the event target identification, the capture/bubble phase traversal, the event listener invocation, and the default action execution.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/firefox--871325b8.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

Perfect! I've successfully completed the analysis of the Firefox DOM event dispatch chain. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've traced the complete DOM event dispatch flow in Firefox, documented in `/workspace/answer.json`. The analysis covers:

### Key Components:
1. **Event Creation** - `EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()` instantiates type-specific DOM events
2. **Event Dispatch Initialization** - `EventDispatcher::Dispatch()` sets up the dispatch process  
3. **Event Target Chain** - `EventTargetChainItem` creates a chain walking up the DOM tree
4. **Three Dispatch Phases**:
   - **Capture Phase** (lines 516-585): Top-down traversal, invoking capture listeners
   - **Target Phase** (lines 587-611): Both capture and bubble listeners on the target element
   - **Bubble Phase** (lines 613-649): Bottom-up traversal, invoking bubble listeners
5. **Listener Invocation** - `EventListenerManager::HandleEventSingleListener()` invokes actual handlers
6. **Default Actions** - `ActivationBehavior` methods execute after listeners (e.g., form submission)
7. **System Event Group** - Re-dispatches for internal Firefox event processing

### Files Identified:
- `dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp/h` - Core dispatch logic
- `dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp/h` - Listener management
- `dom/events/EventTarget.cpp/h` - Base event target class
- `dom/html/HTMLButtonElement.cpp` - Example default action implementation

The answer includes specific file paths, line numbers, and a detailed narrative explaining how each component works together to dispatch DOM events according to the W3C specification.

Iteration happens twice,\n48:  * first for the default event group and then for the system event group.\n49:  * While dispatching the event for the system event group PostHandleEvent\n50:  * is called right after calling event listener for the current event target.\n51:  */\n52: \n53: class MOZ_STACK_CLASS EventChainVisitor {\n54:  public:\n55:   // For making creators of this class instances guarantee the lifetime of\n56:   // aPresContext, this needs to be marked as MOZ_CAN_RUN_SCRIPT.\n57:   MOZ_CAN_RUN_SCRIPT\n58:   EventChainVisitor(nsPresContext* aPresContext, WidgetEvent* aEvent,\n59:                     dom::Event* aDOMEvent,\n60:                     nsEventStatus aEventStatus = nsEventStatus_eIgnore)\n61:       : mPresContext(aPresContext),\n62:         mEvent(aEvent),\n63:         mDOMEvent(aDOMEvent),\n64:         mEventStatus(aEventStatus),\n65:         mItemFlags(0) {}\n66: \n67:   /**\n68:    * The prescontext, possibly nullptr.\n69:    * Note that the lifetime of mPresContext is guaranteed by the creators.\n70:    */\n71:   MOZ_KNOWN_LIVE nsPresContext* const mPresContext;\n72: \n73:   /**\n74:    * The WidgetEvent which is being dispatched. */\n88:   nsEventStatus mEventStatus;\n89: \n90:   /**\n91:    * Bits for items in the event target chain.\n92:    * Set in GetEventTargetParent() and used in PostHandleEvent().\n93:    *\n94:    * @note These bits are different for each item in the event target chain.\n95:    *       It is up to the Pre/PostHandleEvent implementation to decide how to\n96:    *       use these bits.\n97: Capture Phase (lines 516-585 in HandleEventTargetChain)\\n- Sets mInCapturePhase and mInTargetPhase flags on the event\\n- Iterates from the top of the chain down to (but not including) the target\\n- Calls EventTargetChainItem::HandleEvent() on each item\\n- Respects propagation stopped flags and dispatch filters\\n\\n## 5.
